Task instruction sent to agent 
# [VS Code] Fix Stale TypeScript Diagnostics After Git Branch Switch

**Repository:** microsoft/vscode  
**Difficulty:** HARD  
**Category:** big_code_feature
**Task Type:** Feature Implementation - Large Codebase

**Reference:** [Trevor's Big Code Research](../../../docs/TREVOR_RESEARCH_DEC2025.md#1-vs-code-stale-diagnostics-after-git-branch-switch)

## Description

Users are seeing stale TypeScript diagnostics in the Problems panel after switching Git branches. Files that no longer have errors still show the old errors until the user manually opens each file and makes an edit. It seems like the diagnostics pipeline only refreshes on in-editor changes and misses file-on-disk changes from Git operations.

## Task

This task requires implementing code changes to fix stale diagnostics.

### Required Implementation

Check the full diagnostics flow from a text change through the extension host to the Problems view, identify where file system changes should trigger diagnostic updates, and propose where we'd need to add listeners to fix this.

### Implementation Steps

1. **Understand the diagnostics pipeline**:
   - Find the main diagnostics collection and how it stores errors per file
   - Locate the extension host communication for sending diagnostics to the client
   - Find the Problems view panel and how it subscribes to diagnostics
   - Look for existing file change listeners (e.g., `deleteAllDiagnosticsInFile`, `onWillChange`)

2. **Identify where diagnostics are currently refreshed**:
   - Find the text change event handlers that trigger re-diagnostics
   - Understand how the diagnostics pipeline reacts to document changes
   - Look for any existing file system watchers or listeners

3. **Add file system change triggers**:
   - Add listener for file changes on disk (e.g., from `git checkout`)
   - Trigger diagnostics refresh for changed files
   - Clear stale diagnostics for files that no longer exist
   - Re-run TypeScript/language server analysis for affected files

4. **Test the fix**:
   - Switch branches that change TypeScript errors
   - Verify stale diagnostics are cleared
   - Verify new errors are shown after branch switch
   - No duplicate diagnostics appear

5. **Verify no regressions**:
   - All tests pass: `npm test`
   - No performance regression from additional file watchers
   - Diagnostics still work for in-editor changes

## Success Criteria

[x] Stale diagnostics are cleared when files change on disk  
[x] New diagnostics appear after Git branch switch  
[x] Diagnostics refresh without requiring manual file edits  
[x] Problems panel reflects current state of files  
[x] All tests pass: `npm test`  
[x] No performance regression  
[x] Code follows VS Code conventions and patterns  

## Testing

```bash
npm test
```

   177→	changeOne(owner: string, resource: URI, markerData: IMarkerData[]): void {
   178→
   179→		if (isFalsyOrEmpty(markerData)) {
   180→			// remove marker for this (owner,resource)-tuple
   181→			const removed = this._data.delete(resource, owner);
   182→			if (removed) {
   183→				this._onMarkerChanged.fire([resource]);
   184→			}
   185→
   186→		} else {
   187→			// insert marker for this (owner,resource)-tuple
   188→			const markers: IMarker[] = [];
   189→			for (const data of markerData) {
   190→				const marker = MarkerService._toMarker(owner, resource, data);
   191→				if (marker) {
   192→					markers.push(marker);
   193→				}
   194→			}
   195→			this._data.set(resource, owner, markers);
   196→			this._onMarkerChanged.fire([resource]);
   197→		}
   198→	}

Excellent! Now I have all the information needed. Let me create a comprehensive summary document:

## VS Code Diagnostics Pipeline - Complete Architecture Overview

Based on my exploration of the VS Code codebase, here's a comprehensive guide to the diagnostics pipeline, file system handling, and related components:

---

### **1. DIAGNOSTICS PIPELINE**

#### **Extension Host Diagnostics (Client Side)**
**File:** `/workspace/src/vs/workbench/api/common/extHostDiagnostics.ts`

**Purpose:** Manages diagnostic collections created by extensions. This is where extensions set and update diagnostics.

**Key Components:**
- **DiagnosticCollection class**: Stores diagnostics for each URI, with limits on diagnostics per file (1000) and total diagnostics (1100). Converts vscode diagnostics to IMarkerData format.
- **ExtHostDiagnostics class**: Main service that manages all diagnostic collections and provides the public API. Uses a DebounceEmitter (50ms debounce) to batch diagnostic changes before sending to main thread.
- **Flow**: Extension → DiagnosticCollection.set() → Converts to IMarkerData → Calls proxy.$changeMany() → Sends to MainThreadDiagnostics

---

#### **Main Thread Diagnostics (Main Side)**
**File:** `/workspace/src/vs/workbench/api/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.ts`

**Purpose:** Receives diagnostics from extensions and forwards them to the MarkerService on the main thread.

**Key Components:**
- Receives $changeMany() and $clear() calls from ExtHostDiagnostics
- Revives URIs and validates marker data (relatedInformation, code targets)
- Registers markers with IMarkerService via changeOne()
- Tracks active diagnostic owners to prevent circular updates
- Listens to IMarkerService.onMarkerChanged to forward external markers back to extension host via $acceptMarkersCha
... (truncated)

   973→				case FileChangeType.DELETED:
   974→					this.rawDeleted.push(change.resource);
   975→					break;
   976→			}
   977→
   978→			// Figure out events correlation
   979→			if (this.correlationId !== FileChangesEvent.MIXED_CORRELATION) {
   980→				if (typeof change.cId === 'number') {
   981→					if (this.correlationId === undefined) {
   982→						this.correlationId = change.cId; 							// correlation not yet set, just take it
   983→					} else if (this.correlationId !== change.cId) {
   984→						this.correlationId = FileChangesEvent.MIXED_CORRELATION;	// correlation mismatch, we have mixed correlation
   985→					}
   986→				} else {
   987→					if (this.correlationId !== undefined) {
   988→						this.correlationId = FileChangesEvent.MIXED_CORRELATION;	// correlation mismatch, we have mixed correlation
   989→					}
   990→				}
   991→			}
   992→		}
   993→	}
   994→
   995→	private readonly added = new Lazy(() => {
   996→		const added = TernarySearchTree.forUris<boolean>(() => this.ignorePathCasing);
   997→		added.fill(this.rawAdded.map(resource => [resource, true]));
   998→
   999→		return added;

# Simplify: Code Review and Cleanup

Review all changed files for reuse, quality, and efficiency. Fix any issues found.

## Phase 1: Identify Changes

Run `git diff` (or `git diff HEAD` if there are staged changes) to see what changed. If there are no git changes, review the most recently modified files that the user mentioned or that you edited earlier in this conversation.

## Phase 2: Launch Three Review Agents in Parallel

Use the Agent tool to launch all three agents concurrently in a single message. Pass each agent the full diff so it has the complete context.

### Agent 1: Code Reuse Review

For each change:

1. **Search for existing utilities and helpers** that could replace newly written code. Use Grep to find similar patterns elsewhere in the codebase — common locations are utility directories, shared modules, and files adjacent to the changed ones.
2. **Flag any new function that duplicates existing functionality.** Suggest the existing function to use instead.
3. **Flag any inline logic that could use an existing utility** — hand-rolled string manipulation, manual path handling, custom environment checks, ad-hoc type guards, and similar patterns are common candidates.

### Agent 2: Code Quality Review

Review the same changes for hacky patterns:

1. **Redundant state**: state that duplicates existing state, cached values that could be derived, observers/effects that could be direct calls
2. **Parameter sprawl**: adding new parameters to a function instead of generalizing or restructuring existing ones
3. **Copy-paste with slight variation**: near-duplicate code blocks that should be unified with a shared abstraction
4. **Leaky abstractions**: exposing internal details that should be encapsulated, or breaking existing abstraction boundaries
5. **Stringly-type

 		}
 	}
 
+	private _onDidFilesChange(event: any): void {
+		// Clear diagnostics for updated and deleted files to allow re-analysis
+		const filesToClear = new Set<string>();
+
+		// Collect updated files
+		for (const resource of event.rawUpdated ?? []) {
+			filesToClear.add(this._uriIdentService.asCanonicalUri(resource).toString());
+		}
+
+		// Collect deleted files
+		for (const resource of event.rawDeleted ?? []) {
+			filesToClear.add(this._uriIdentService.asCanonicalUri(resource).toString());
+		}
+
+		// Clear diagnostics for all affected files
+		if (filesToClear.size > 0) {
+			const owners = new Set<string>();
+			for (const uriStr of filesToClear) {
+				const uri = URI.parse(uriStr);
+				const markers = this._markerService.read({ resource: uri });
+				for (const marker of markers) {
+					owners.add(marker.owner);
+				}
+			}
+
+			// Clear all diagnostics for affected files and owners
+			for (const uriStr of filesToClear) {
+				const uri = URI.parse(uriStr);
+				for (const owner of owners) {
+					this._markerService.changeOne(owner, uri, []);
+				}
+			}
+		}
+	}
```

Look for:
1. Type safety issues (event: any should be typed properly)
2. Leaky abstractions - are internal event properties being accessed?
3. Redundant state or duplicate logic

+		// Collect deleted files
+		for (const resource of event.rawDeleted ?? []) {
+			filesToClear.add(this._uriIdentService.asCanonicalUri(resource).toString());
+		}
+
+		// Clear diagnostics for all affected files
+		if (filesToClear.size > 0) {
+			const owners = new Set<string>();
+			for (const uriStr of filesToClear) {
+				const uri = URI.parse(uriStr);
+				const markers = this._markerService.read({ resource: uri });
+				for (const marker of markers) {
+					owners.add(marker.owner);
+				}
+			}
+
+			// Clear all diagnostics for affected files and owners
+			for (const uriStr of filesToClear) {
+				const uri = URI.parse(uriStr);
+				for (const owner of owners) {
+					this._markerService.changeOne(owner, uri, []);
+				}
+			}
+		}
+	}
```

Look for:
1. Unnecessary work or redundant computations
2. Inefficient data structure conversions (string <-> URI conversions)
3. Nested loops that could be optimized
4. Hot-path performance concerns
5. Missing early returns or short-circuit logic
6. N+1 pattern issues

Report specific performance concerns with suggestions.

   963→		for (const change of changes) {
   964→

   968→					this.rawAdded.push(change.resource);
   969→					break;
   970→				case FileChangeType.UPDATED:
   971→					this.rawUpdated.push(change.resource);
   972→					break;
   973→				case FileChangeType.DELETED:
   974→					this.rawDeleted.push(change.resource);
   975→					break;
   976→			}
   977→
   978→			// Figure out events correlation
   979→			if (this.correlationId !== FileChangesEvent.MIXED_CORRELATION) {
   980→				if (typeof change.cId === 'number') {
   981→					if (this.correlationId === undefined) {
   982→						this.correlationId = change.cId; 							// correlation not yet set, just take it
   983→					} else if (this.correlationId !== change.cId) {
   984→						this.correlationId = FileChangesEvent.MIXED_CORRELATION;	// correlation mismatch, we have mixed correlation
   985→					}
   986→				} else {
   987→					if (this.correlationId !== undefined) {
   988→						this.correlationId = FileChangesEvent.MIXED_CORRELATION;	// correlation mismatch, we have mixed correlation
   989→					}
   990→				}
   991→			}
   992→		}

## Performance and Efficiency Issues Analysis

I've reviewed the `_onDidFilesChange` method in `/workspace/src/vs/workbench/api/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.ts` (lines 60-93) and identified several significant efficiency issues:

### Critical Performance Issues

#### 1. **Double String-to-URI Conversion (N+1 Pattern)**
**Severity: HIGH**

The code converts URI strings back to URI objects twice, doubling the parsing work:

```typescript
// First loop: String -> URI (line 78)
const uri = URI.parse(uriStr);
const markers = this._markerService.read({ resource: uri });

// Second loop: String -> URI again (line 87)
const uri = URI.parse(uriStr);
for (const owner of owners) {
    this._markerService.changeOne(owner, uri, []);
}
```

**Impact**: If there are 100 changed files and 5 owners, this performs 200 `URI.parse()` operations instead of 100.

**Recommendation**: Store URI objects instead of strings:
```typescript
const filesToClear = new Map<string, URI>(); // Map string keys to URI objects

for (const resource of event.rawUpdated ?? []) {
    const uri = this._uriIdentService.asCanonicalUri(resource);
    filesToClear.set(uri.toString(), uri);
}
```

---

#### 2. **Two-Pass Algorithm (O(n*m) Nested Loop)**
**Severity: HIGH**

The code iterates over `filesToClear` twice:
- **First pass** (lines 77-83): Collects all unique owner names
- **Second pass** (lines 86-91): Clears markers for each (owner, file) combination

This creates an O(n*m) pattern where `n` = files and `m` = unique owners.

**Example scenario**: 100 changed files with 10 unique diagnostic owners = 1,000 `changeOne()` calls instead of the optimal 100.

**Recommendation**: Combine into a si

## Code Quality Review: mainThreadDiagnostics.ts

I've identified several significant code quality issues in the `_onDidFilesChange` method:

### **Critical Issues**

#### 1. **Type Safety: `event: any` Parameter (Line 60)**
- **Severity:** High
- **Issue:** The parameter is typed as `any`, which defeats TypeScript's type checking
- **Location:** `private _onDidFilesChange(event: any): void {`
- **Fix:** The `IFileService.onDidFilesChange` event signature expects `FileChangesEvent`, not `any`
  ```typescript
  // Current (unsafe):
  private _onDidFilesChange(event: any): void {
  
  // Should be:
  private _onDidFilesChange(event: FileChangesEvent): void {
  ```
- **Impact:** Loses compile-time validation and IDE intellisense support. Accessing non-existent properties would silently fail.

- **Why It's Bad:** The deprecation exists because these properties require expensive lookups. The class provides optimized methods (`contains()`, `affects()`) that should be used instead

## Code Reuse Analysis: mainThreadDiagnostics.ts Diff

I've reviewed the git diff and searched the codebase for existing utilities and patterns. Here are my findings:

### 1. **Missed Opportunity: IMarkerService.remove() Method**

**Location:** `/workspace/src/vs/platform/markers/common/markerService.ts` (lines 171-175)

The IMarkerService already has a dedicated `remove()` method that is purpose-built for clearing markers from multiple resources:

```typescript
remove(owner: string, resources: URI[]): void {
	for (const resource of resources || []) {
		this.changeOne(owner, resource, []);
	}
}
```

**Current Code Issue:** The new `_onDidFilesChange()` method (lines 74-92 in the diff) manually loops through resources and calls `changeOne()` for each owner/resource pair. This duplicates the logic already in the `remove()` method.

**Recommendation:** The diagnostic clearing logic could be simplified significantly using `remove()` instead of nested loops.

---

### 2. **Inefficient URI String Conversion Pattern**

**Location:** Lines 65-72 in the diff

The code converts URIs to strings unnecessarily:

```typescript
// Current pattern (inefficient)

    filesToClear.add(this._uriIdentService.asCanonicalUri(resource).toString());
}

// Then later:
for (const uriStr of filesToClear) {
    const uri = URI.parse(uriStr);  // Converting back to URI!
}
```

**Better Alternative:** Use `ResourceSet` from `/workspace/src/vs/base/common/map.ts` (line 153), which is designed specific

- After: 23 lines in _onDidFilesChange method

29bd685 Fix stale TypeScript diagnostics after Git branch switch
315-assistanttext-
## Summary

I've successfully implemented a fix for stale TypeScript diagnostics after Git branch switches. Here's what was completed:

### **Implementation Overview**

The fix adds a file system change listener to `MainThreadDiagnostics` that clears stale diagnostics when files change on disk, allowing language servers to re-analyze and provide updated diagnostics.

### **Key Changes**

1. **`/workspace/src/vs/workbench/api/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.ts`**
   - Injected `IFileService` dependency
   - Subscribed to `onDidFilesChange` events in constructor
   - Implemented `_onDidFilesChange()` method to clear diagnostics for updated/deleted files
   - Proper resource cleanup in `dispose()` method

2. **`/workspace/src/vs/workbench/api/test/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.test.ts`**
   - Updated all 5 `MainThreadDiagnostics` instantiations to provide `IFileService` mock
   - Added 2 new tests: `clear diagnostics on file changes` and `clear diagnostics on file deletion`

### **Code Review Improvements Applied**

✅ **Type Safety**: Changed `event: any` to `event: FileChangesEvent` for compile-time validation

✅ **Performance**: Reduced from O(n*m) two-pass to single-pass O(n + Σmarkers) algorithm

✅ **Memory**: Eliminated redundant URI.parse()/toString() conversions

✅ **Clarity**: Only clears diagnostics that actually exist for each file

✅ **Code Quality**: Reduced method from 37 to 23 lines (36% reduction)

### **How It Works**

1. When files change on disk (git checkout), `IFileService` fires `onDidFilesChange`
2. The new handler collects updated and deleted files
3. For each file, it reads existing diagnostic markers from the `MarkerService`
4. Clears all those diagnostics to allow re-analysis
5. Language servers re-analyze and set new (correct) diagnostics

KEY PATTERNS & INSIGHTS**\n\n1. **Debouncing**: Both diagnostic changes (50ms) and marker service events use debouncing to batch updates efficiently\n\n2. **Event-Driven**: The entire system is event-driven with clear separation of concerns via service interfaces\n\n3. **Correlation IDs**: File watcher and marker services use correlation IDs to track related operations together\n\n4. **Dual Indexing**: MarkerService uses DoubleResourceMap to index by both resource and owner for efficient lookups\n\n5. **RPC Protocol**: Clear request/response separation between extension host and main thread with well-defined shapes\n\n6. **Filtering**: Multiple layers of filtering (unsupported schemas, file.exclude, severity levels, search text)\n\n7. **URI Normalization**: Extensive use of extUri for case-sensitive/insensitive comparisons across platforms\n\nThis architecture enables VS Code to efficiently handle thousands of diagnostics from multiple extensions while maintaining responsiveness through intelligent batching and filtering.",

  "content": "# VS Code Diagnostics Fix - Stale Diagnostics After Git Branch Switch\n\n## Problem\nUsers see stale TypeScript diagnostics after switching Git branches. Files that no longer have errors still show old errors until manually opened.\n\n## Root Cause\n- Diagnostics are stored in `MarkerService` (central repository)\n- When files change on disk (git checkout), file system fires `onDidFilesChange` event\n- **No listener** exists to clear stale diagnostics when files change on disk\n- Diagnostics only refresh on in-editor text changes\n\n## Solution Architecture\n1. Add file system change listener to `MainThreadDiagnostics`\n2. When `IFileService.onDidFilesChange` fires, clear diagnostics for changed files\n3. This allows extensions to re-analyze and set new diagnostics\n\n## Key Files\n- `/workspace/src/vs/workbench/api/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.ts` - RPC handler for extension diagnostics\n- `/workspace/src/vs/platform/files/common/fileService.ts` - File system provider and change events\n- `/workspace/src/vs/platform/markers/common/markerService.ts` - Central diagnostic storage\n- `/workspace/src/vs/workbench/api/test/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.test.ts` - Tests\n\n## Implementation Steps\n1. Inject `IFileService` into `MainThreadDiagnostics`\n2. Subscribe to `onDidFilesChange` event\n3. For each changed file, clear all diagnostics in that file\n4. This allows re-analysis on file changes\n",

- Duplicates the URI parsing logic\n  - The second iteration calls `changeOne` for every (owner, uri) combination, which could be inefficient\n  - Logic could be consolidated into a single FileChangesEvent): void {\n    // Only process if there are changes to handle\n    if (!event.gotUpdated() && !event.gotDeleted()) {\n        return;\n    }\n    \n    // Collect affected files\n filesToClear) {\n        const markers = this._markerService.read({ resource: uri });\n        const uniqueOwners = new Set(markers.map(m => m.owner));\n        \n        for (const owner of uniqueOwners) {\n            this._markerService.changeOne(owner, uri, []);\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Alternative (using recommended event methods):**\nNote that this requires more significant []) {\n    const uri = this._uriIdentService.asCanonicalUri(resource);\n    filesToClear.set(uri.toString(), uri);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n#### 2. **Two-Pass Algorithm (O(n*m) Nested Loop)**\n**Severity: HIGH**\n\nThe code iterates over `filesToClear` twice:\n- **First pass** (lines 77-83): Collects all unique owner names\n- **Second pass** (lines 86-91): Clears markers for each (owner, file) combination\n\nThis creates an O(n*m) pattern where `n` = files and `m` = unique owners.\n\n**Example scenario**: 100 changed files with 10 unique diagnostic owners = 1,000 `changeOne()` calls instead of the optimal 100.\n\n**Recommendation**: Combine into a single pass structure using a Map:\n```typescript\nconst filesToClearWithOwners = new Map<string, Set<string>>();\n// First pass: collect owners per file\nfor (const [uriStr, uri] of filesToClear) {\n    const markers = this._markerService.read({ resource: uri });\n    const owners = new Set(markers.map(m => m.owner));\n    filesToClearWithOwners.set(uriStr, owners);\n}\n\n// Second pass: clear exactly what's needed\nfor (const [uriStr, owners] of filesToClearWithOwners) {\n    const uri = URI.parse(uriStr);\n    for (const owner of owners) {\n        this._markerService.changeOne(owner, uri, []);\n    }\n}\n```\n\nWhile this still has the loop structure, it at least collects data efficiently.\n\n---\n\n#### 3. **Unnecessary Iteration Over Diagnostic Owners**\n**Severity: MEDIUM**\n\nThe code collects ALL unique owners across all files, then clears diagnostics for EVERY owner on EVERY file, even if that owner never had diagnostics on that file:\n\n```typescript\n// Collects owners globally\nconst owners = new Set<string>();\nfor (const uriStr of filesToClear) {\n    const uri = URI.parse(uriStr);\n    const markers = this._markerService.read({ resource: uri });\n    for (const marker of markers) {\n        owners.add(marker.owner); Files that no longer have errors still show old errors until manually opened.\n\n## Root Cause\n- Diagnostics are stored in `MarkerService` (central repository)\n- When files change on disk (git checkout), file system fires `onDidFilesChange` event\n- **No listener** exists to clear stale diagnostics when files change on disk\n- Diagnostics only refresh on in-editor text changes\n\n## Solution Implemented\n1. \u2705 Added file system change listener to `MainThreadDiagnostics`\n2. \u2705 Type-safe event handling with `FileChangesEvent` parameter\n3. \u2705 Single-pass algorithm: clear only diagnostics that actually exist\n4. \u2705 No unnecessary string/URI conversions\n5. \u2705 Added tests for file update and deletion scenarios\n\n## Key Changes Made\n- File: `/workspace/src/vs/workbench/api/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.ts`\n  - Injected `IFileService` dependency\n  - Subscribed to `onDidFilesChange` events\n  - Implemented `_onDidFilesChange()` with optimized single-pass clearing\n  - Properly typed event as `FileChangesEvent` (not `any`)\n  - Stores URIs directly in Set<URI> (no string conversions)\n\n- File: `/workspace/src/vs/workbench/api/test/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.test.ts`\n  - Added two new tests: `clear diagnostics on file changes` and `clear diagnostics on file deletion`\n  - All existing tests updated to provide IFileService mock\n\n## Performance Improvements\n- Algorithm: O(n*m) \u2192 O(n + \u03a3markers)\n- Eliminated URI.parse()/toString() round-trips\n- Single-pass iteration instead of two-pass\n- Only clears owners that actually have diagnostics on each file\n- Code size: 37 lines \u2192 23 lines (-36%)",

1. WRITE /logs/agent/sessions/projects/-workspace/memory/MEMORY.md
# VS Code Diagnostics Fix - Stale Diagnostics After Git Branch Switch

## Problem
Users see stale TypeScript diagnostics after switching Git branches. Files that no longer have errors still show old errors until manually opened.

## Root Cause
- Diagnostics are stored in `MarkerService` (central repository)
- When files change on disk (git checkout), file system fires `onDidFilesChange` event
- **No listener** exists to clear stale diagnostics when files change on disk
- Diagnostics only refresh on in-editor text changes

## Solution Architecture
1. Add file system change listener to `MainThreadDiagnostics`
2. When `IFileService.onDidFilesChange` fires, clear diagnostics for changed files
3. This allows extensions to re-analyze and set new diagnostics

## Key Files
- `/workspace/src/vs/workbench/api/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.ts` - RPC handler for extension diagnostics
- `/workspace/src/vs/platform/files/common/fileService.ts` - File system provider and change events
- `/workspace/src/vs/platform/markers/common/markerService.ts` - Central diagnostic storage
- `/workspace/src/vs/workbench/api/test/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.test.ts` - Tests

## Implementation Steps
1. Inject `IFileService` into `MainThreadDiagnostics`
2. Subscribe to `onDidFilesChange` event
3. For each changed file, clear all diagnostics in that file
4. This allows re-analysis on file changes

@extHostNamedCustomer(MainContext.MainThreadDiagnostics)
export class MainThreadDiagnostics implements MainThreadDiagnosticsShape {

	private readonly _activeOwners = new Set<string>();

	private readonly _proxy: ExtHostDiagnosticsShape;
	private readonly _markerListener: IDisposable;
	private readonly _fileListener: IDisposable;

	constructor(
		extHostContext: IExtHostContext,
		@IMarkerService private readonly _markerService: IMarkerService,
		@IUriIdentityService private readonly _uriIdentService: IUriIdentityService,
		@IFileService private readonly _fileService: IFileService,
	) {
		this._proxy = extHostContext.getProxy(ExtHostContext.ExtHostDiagnostics);

		this._markerListener = this._markerService.onMarkerChanged(this._forwardMarkers, this);
		this._fileListener = this._fileService.onDidFilesChange(this._onDidFilesChange, this);
	}

5. EDIT /workspace/src/vs/workbench/api/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.ts
Before
	private _forwardMarkers(resources: readonly URI[]): void {
		const data: [UriComponents, IMarkerData[]][] = [];
		for (const resource of resources) {
			const allMarkerData = this._markerService.read({ resource });
			if (allMarkerData.length === 0) {
				data.push([resource, []]);
			} else {
				const forgeinMarkerData = allMarkerData.filter(marker => !this._activeOwners.has(marker.owner));
				if (forgeinMarkerData.length > 0) {
					data.push([resource, forgeinMarkerData]);
				}
			}
		}
		if (data.length > 0) {
			this._proxy.$acceptMarkersChange(data);
		}
	}
After
	private _forwardMarkers(resources: readonly URI[]): void {
		const data: [UriComponents, IMarkerData[]][] = [];
		for (const resource of resources) {
			const allMarkerData = this._markerService.read({ resource });
			if (allMarkerData.length === 0) {
				data.push([resource, []]);
			} else {
				const forgeinMarkerData = allMarkerData.filter(marker => !this._activeOwners.has(marker.owner));
				if (forgeinMarkerData.length > 0) {
					data.push([resource, forgeinMarkerData]);
				}
			}
		}
		if (data.length > 0) {
			this._proxy.$acceptMarkersChange(data);
		}
	}

	private _onDidFilesChange(event: any): void {
		// Clear diagnostics for updated and deleted files to allow re-analysis
		const filesToClear: URI[] = [];

		// Collect updated files
		for (const resource of event.rawUpdated ?? []) {
			filesToClear.push(resource);
		}

		// Collect deleted files
		for (const resource of event.rawDeleted ?? []) {
			filesToClear.push(resource);
		}

		// Clear diagnostics for all affected files and all owners
		for (const uri of filesToClear) {
			const canonicalUri = this._uriIdentService.asCanonicalUri(uri);
			const markers = this._markerService.read({ resource: canonicalUri });
			for (const marker of markers) {
				this._markerService.changeOne(marker.owner, canonicalUri, []);
			}
		}
	}
6. EDIT /workspace/src/vs/workbench/api/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.ts
Before
	private _onDidFilesChange(event: any): void {
		// Clear diagnostics for updated and deleted files to allow re-analysis
		const filesToClear: URI[] = [];

		// Collect updated files
		for (const resource of event.rawUpdated ?? []) {
			filesToClear.push(resource);
		}

		// Collect deleted files
		for (const resource of event.rawDeleted ?? []) {
			filesToClear.push(resource);
		}

		// Clear diagnostics for all affected files and all owners
		for (const uri of filesToClear) {
			const canonicalUri = this._uriIdentService.asCanonicalUri(uri);
			const markers = this._markerService.read({ resource: canonicalUri });
			for (const marker of markers) {
				this._markerService.changeOne(marker.owner, canonicalUri, []);
			}
		}
	}
After
	private _onDidFilesChange(event: any): void {
		// Clear diagnostics for updated and deleted files to allow re-analysis
		const filesToClear = new Set<string>();

		// Collect updated files
		for (const resource of event.rawUpdated ?? []) {
			filesToClear.add(this._uriIdentService.asCanonicalUri(resource).toString());
		}

		// Collect deleted files
		for (const resource of event.rawDeleted ?? []) {
			filesToClear.add(this._uriIdentService.asCanonicalUri(resource).toString());
		}

		// Clear diagnostics for all affected files
		if (filesToClear.size > 0) {
			const owners = new Set<string>();
			for (const uriStr of filesToClear) {
				const uri = URI.parse(uriStr);
				const markers = this._markerService.read({ resource: uri });
				for (const marker of markers) {
					owners.add(marker.owner);
				}
			}

			// Clear all diagnostics for affected files and owners
			for (const uriStr of filesToClear) {
				const uri = URI.parse(uriStr);
				for (const owner of owners) {
					this._markerService.changeOne(owner, uri, []);
				}
			}
		}
	}

	test('onDidChangeDiagnostics different behavior when "extensionKind" ui running on remote workspace #136955', function () {
		return runWithFakedTimers({}, async () => {

				code: '666',
				startLineNumber: 1,
				startColumn: 1,
				endLineNumber: 1,
				endColumn: 1,
				severity: 1,
				source: 'me',
				message: 'message'

					remoteAuthority = '';
					extensionHostKind = ExtensionHostKind.LocalProcess;
					dispose() { }
					assertRegistered() { }

						return {

								changedData.push(data);

13. EDIT /workspace/src/vs/workbench/api/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.ts
Before
	private _onDidFilesChange(event: any): void {
		// Clear diagnostics for updated and deleted files to allow re-analysis
		const filesToClear = new Set<string>();

		// Collect updated files
		for (const resource of event.rawUpdated ?? []) {
			filesToClear.add(this._uriIdentService.asCanonicalUri(resource).toString());
		}

		// Collect deleted files
		for (const resource of event.rawDeleted ?? []) {
			filesToClear.add(this._uriIdentService.asCanonicalUri(resource).toString());
		}

		// Clear diagnostics for all affected files
		if (filesToClear.size > 0) {
			const owners = new Set<string>();
			for (const uriStr of filesToClear) {
				const uri = URI.parse(uriStr);
				const markers = this._markerService.read({ resource: uri });
				for (const marker of markers) {
					owners.add(marker.owner);
				}
			}

			// Clear all diagnostics for affected files and owners
			for (const uriStr of filesToClear) {
				const uri = URI.parse(uriStr);
				for (const owner of owners) {
					this._markerService.changeOne(owner, uri, []);
				}
			}
		}
	}
After
	private _onDidFilesChange(event: FileChangesEvent): void {
		// Clear diagnostics for updated and deleted files to allow re-analysis
		const filesToClear = new Set<URI>();

		// Collect updated files
		for (const resource of event.rawUpdated) {
			filesToClear.add(this._uriIdentService.asCanonicalUri(resource));
		}

		// Collect deleted files
		for (const resource of event.rawDeleted) {
			filesToClear.add(this._uriIdentService.asCanonicalUri(resource));
		}

		// Clear diagnostics for affected files: single-pass iteration
		// Only clear owners that actually have diagnostics on each file
		for (const uri of filesToClear) {
			const markers = this._markerService.read({ resource: uri });
			for (const marker of markers) {
				this._markerService.changeOne(marker.owner, uri, []);
			}
		}
	}
14. EDIT /logs/agent/sessions/projects/-workspace/memory/MEMORY.md
Before
# VS Code Diagnostics Fix - Stale Diagnostics After Git Branch Switch

## Problem
Users see stale TypeScript diagnostics after switching Git branches. Files that no longer have errors still show old errors until manually opened.

## Root Cause
- Diagnostics are stored in `MarkerService` (central repository)
- When files change on disk (git checkout), file system fires `onDidFilesChange` event
- **No listener** exists to clear stale diagnostics when files change on disk
- Diagnostics only refresh on in-editor text changes

## Solution Architecture
1. Add file system change listener to `MainThreadDiagnostics`
2. When `IFileService.onDidFilesChange` fires, clear diagnostics for changed files
3. This allows extensions to re-analyze and set new diagnostics

## Key Files
- `/workspace/src/vs/workbench/api/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.ts` - RPC handler for extension diagnostics
- `/workspace/src/vs/platform/files/common/fileService.ts` - File system provider and change events
- `/workspace/src/vs/platform/markers/common/markerService.ts` - Central diagnostic storage
- `/workspace/src/vs/workbench/api/test/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.test.ts` - Tests

## Implementation Steps
1. Inject `IFileService` into `MainThreadDiagnostics`
2. Subscribe to `onDidFilesChange` event
3. For each changed file, clear all diagnostics in that file
4. This allows re-analysis on file changes
After
# VS Code Diagnostics Fix - Stale Diagnostics After Git Branch Switch

## Problem
Users see stale TypeScript diagnostics after switching Git branches. Files that no longer have errors still show old errors until manually opened.

## Root Cause
- Diagnostics are stored in `MarkerService` (central repository)
- When files change on disk (git checkout), file system fires `onDidFilesChange` event
- **No listener** exists to clear stale diagnostics when files change on disk
- Diagnostics only refresh on in-editor text changes

## Solution Implemented
1. ✅ Added file system change listener to `MainThreadDiagnostics`
2. ✅ Type-safe event handling with `FileChangesEvent` parameter
3. ✅ Single-pass algorithm: clear only diagnostics that actually exist
4. ✅ No unnecessary string/URI conversions
5. ✅ Added tests for file update and deletion scenarios

## Key Changes Made
- File: `/workspace/src/vs/workbench/api/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.ts`
  - Injected `IFileService` dependency
  - Subscribed to `onDidFilesChange` events
  - Implemented `_onDidFilesChange()` with optimized single-pass clearing
  - Properly typed event as `FileChangesEvent` (not `any`)
  - Stores URIs directly in Set<URI> (no string conversions)

- File: `/workspace/src/vs/workbench/api/test/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.test.ts`
  - Added two new tests: `clear diagnostics on file changes` and `clear diagnostics on file deletion`
  - All existing tests updated to provide IFileService mock

## Performance Improvements
- Algorithm: O(n*m) → O(n + Σmarkers)
- Eliminated URI.parse()/toString() round-trips
- Single-pass iteration instead of two-pass
- Only clears owners that actually have diagnostics on each file
- Code size: 37 lines → 23 lines (-36%)
